A.1.5
Medical Laboratory Technologist at Sjællands Universitetshospital,
Roskilde - Region Sjælland
Jeg er bioanalytiker, og har været i afdelingen i 10 år, og i specialet har jeg været i 20 år.
Hvordan udføres en standard EEG-undersøgelse?
Når vi laver selve optagelsen, når der er sat alle de her elektroder på, og orienteret pa-
tienten om undersøgelsen, vi har også det der med, at man lige spørger, hvornår har du
haft dit sidste anfald, har du spist morgenmad, det er i forhold til for eksempel hyperventi-
lationen. Men ellers kommer vi til at sidde bagved skærmen, hvor jeg altid vil starte med
lige at lave sådan lille notits om, det gør vi alle sammen, hvor vi angiver om patienten er
vågen, sovende, er de konfuse, er de orienteret i tid og sted. Vigtigst af alt, er de i deres
habituelle tilstand. Tit når vi kommer i ambulatoriet, så er det patienter, der kommer hjem-
mefra, men vi tager jo også ud og laver akut undersøgelser, og der er det her, det er ret
vigtigt at vide om patienten, er det normalt, at de måske ikke er orienteret i tid og sted,
eller er de lige midt i deres sygdomstilfælde. Så det er ret vigtigt for at kunne vurdere et
EEG, er patienten vågen eller er de sovende.
Så fortæller vi bare lidt om, hvilke elektroder vi har brugt, om de har lukket øjne, åbnet
øjne, om de for eksempel ligger på ryggen eller ligger på siden. Det har noget at gøre
med i forhold til artefakter, altså støj fra kurven, hvis de nu ligger på siden, jamen så
kan vi måske forvente, at der kommer lidt for eksempel bevæge artefakter over fra den
side, de ligger på. Så det starter man lige med at sætte sådan et lille event i starten af
optagelsen, så ved lægen, den der skal sidde og kigge den igennem, lidt om patienten.
Vi har selvfølgelig også henvisningen, vi kan gå fra, men det er faktisk i det øjeblik, når
patienten træder ind af døren. Så skriver vi også altid, hvor den er optaget henne, og
hvem der har gjort det. Når så optagelsen kører, jeg tror, at der er lidt forskel med, hvor
meget men man markerer selvfølgelig altid, hvornår de har øjnene åbne, og hvornår de
har lukket.
Hvordan noterer i artefakter?
Det er jo tit noget, vi beder dem om, for at vurdere reaktiviteten, så der sætter vi et event
ind, og det er jo så auto defineret, altså der er sådan nogle typiske events, der er auto
defineret, dem vi bruger meget. Og så har vi sådan en OBS, hvor vi selv kan skrive, altså
frihånds tekst. Men det er jo så det igen, det der med, at for at det ikke skal mistolkes
som måske noget anfalds aktivitet, så der kan det være vigtigt at skrive events ind. Også
når de bevæger sig, men der har vi selvfølgelig også nogle events til dem, hvis de måske
hoster eller noget. Men det kan jo være forskelligt fra afdeling til afdeling, det er noget,
man selv laver et setup med. Så det kan jo godt være, at på Filadelfia har de valgt nogle
andre events, og en anden rækkefølge, så det er ikke noget, der er prædefineret fra pro-
grammets side af. Vi har så også forskellige paletter, så man kan skifte imellem, så denne
her, den kører vi med i ambulatoriet, og så har vi måske en fra vores søvn optagelser,
og så har vi også en, hvis vi er ude på nogle sengeafsnit, altså nogle akutte afdelinger,
142
Data-driven optimization of UI & UX
==PAGE:150==
intensiv og sådan nogle. Så har vi et andet event, men det er, fordi vi går ud og skal også
lave noget smerte stimulering i forhold til igen for at se meget af denne her reaktivitet. Så
dem sætter vi ind løbende efter behov, man kan også sætte dem ind bagefter, når vi har
kørt optagelsen. Det er selvfølgelig svært på sådan en, hvor den kører løbende, men det
kunne måske være meget godt at kunne sige “hov, nu bevæger patienten sig”, og man
lige sætter et event, og siger “okay, her der er noget uro og bevægelse”, fordi så bliver
det ihvertfald ikke mistolket. Så det er jo også det, vi sidder hele tiden og overvåger, så
selvom vi har video på patienten, så vil vi stadigvæk gå ind og sætte ind, hvis der sker
nogle ting undervejs.
Så er der jo også det her, der er impedans målingerne. Den vil altid være gemt, og hvis
man måler impedansen i løbet af optagelsen, så bliver den også gemt, så man kan gå
ind og præcist se, hvad impedansen var på det givne tidspunkt, og det er bare for at
kvalitetssikrer og dokumentere at alle elektroderne sidder fast.
Vi har sådan et threshold, og her kan man se, at der står, at den er på 10 kOhm, så hvis
de er under 10 kOhm, så vil de være grønne, og hvis de er over 10 kOhm, så bliver de
røde. Så det er bare sådan et hurtigt visuelt overblik, men vi kigger selvfølgelig også lige
på tallene og ser, og hvis der så er en, der er 10.1 kOhm, det er sådan lige på grænsen.
I bund og grund skal impedanserne bare være ensartede, altså helst ikke varierer for
meget, så man ikke har en, der er på fem og en, der er på 15, fordi det kan nemlig også
give noget støj artefakt, så det er faktisk derfor. Hvis man kunne få alle impedanserne til
at være lige omkring 15, så ville det faktisk også være okay, det siger lidt omkring, hvor
godt elektroderne har fat, men det vigtigste er faktisk, at der ikke er for stort spring imellem
dem. Det kan give, hvis vi har for eksempel FZ, der lå på 15 eller 20, jamen så kunne det
godt være, den har jo stadigvæk lidt fat, men der vil være meget støj, der ville komme på
den. Fordi den har så meget forskel i impedansen i forhold til de andre elektroder.
Det hedder sådan helt efter forskrifterne, så tjekker man det altid i starten af kurven, og
man bør også tjekke dem i slutningen af kurven ligesom for at dokumentere, jamen sidder
elektroderne stadigvæk fast. Fordi hvis nu, der er en elektrode, der bliver lidt høj, så kan
den godt blive lidt ustabil på kurven. Hvis den så bliver ustabil, så vil der kunne komme
noget støj på, men der vil også kunne komme nogle forskellige frekvenser, hvor man
ikke rigtig ved, “er det på grund af, at hjernen genererer det, eller er det på grund af, at
elektroden den er ved måske at slippe lidt, og måske impedansen er for høj?” Det er jo lidt
af et problem, man skal helst gerne dokumenterer, hvis du måler impedansen til slut, og
kan se, “jamen, alle impedanser de er grønne, ergo må det være noget, der kommer fra
hjernen, hvis der er en elektrode, der ser lidt pudsig ud”. Men er der så lige den elektrode,
som der måske kommer en uregelmæssig aktivitet på, og lige den elektrode, den har en
høj impedans, jamen så må vi sige, at det er elektroden, der er defekt. Men det har man
ikke en ærlig chance for at vurdere, hvis du kun måler i starten af optagelsen. Jeg tror
bare ikke, der er så mange, der måler til slut i optagelsen, men ifølge ihvertfald mange
forskrifter, der er det ihvertfald anbefalet, at man måler impedanser til slut i optagelsen.
Data-driven optimization of UI & UX
143
==PAGE:151==
Man kan godt måle undervejs, det kan være sådan noget, hvis patienten lige har løftet sig,
og løftet hovedet en gang og så lægger sig ned igen. Så vil man gerne lige tjekke, “sidder
de alle sammen nu stadigvæk fast”. Jeg tror, at det er nok individuelt, man kan godt køre
en hel optagelse uden, hvis patienten bare ligger helt stille, så er der ingen grund til måske
at måle impedansen før til slut i kurven. Men selvom de ligger helt stille, så er der så bare
nogle, som godt kan løsne sig lidt alligevel. Men der ville man måske måle, hvis man
kan se i EEG’et, at så ville man måske lige lave en kontrol, er det elektroden, eller er det
patienten?

Standard EEG and Standard Control EEG Scan

A.2.1
Standard EEG Scan, woman, 77 years old, 29/9/22
• Patient is asked for their CPR number.
• Patient is asked if they know why they are here, and how they feel their symptoms.
• Explains to the patient why they are here and the examination.
• Patient is asked about their medical history, if they have heart problems.
• Shows the equipment to the patient.
• Patient is asked to lay down on the bed.
• Neurophysiology Assistant uses their hands to measure the patient’s scalp in terms
of the 10-20 system.
• Neurophysiology Assistant has chosen to go with loose electrodes rather than a cap
to get some training using it.
• Hair is very noisy (artifact).
• Neurophysiology Assistant firstly puts couple of the electrodes, then REF and GND.
• Neurophysiology Assistant has a device connected to the electrodes which gives
a visual overview of the impedance and connection of the electrodes. The device
uses small lights for each electrode which are all switched on - light means no con-
nection/high impedance whereas no light means a good connection/low impedance.
• Neurophysiology Assistant focuses on having the cords turning the same way, so
they go backwards.
• Patient is asked to move their head for better access to put the electrodes.
• “It’s important to lay down the hair completely or else the electrodes can’t connect”.
• Neurophysiology Assistant scratches the scalp harshly to get a better connection.
• Neurophysiology Assistant has a lot and very good patient communication through-
out.
• Neurophysiology Assistant puts extra six electrodes - also known as low row.
• Neurophysiology Assistant firstly puts electrodes on the left side of the patient’s head
and then moves on to the right side.
• Neurophysiology Assistant has put the threshold at 5 kOhm, and has the ability to
change this if they wish to.

• “The better the preliminary analysis, the better the result for analysis for diagnosis”.
• Neurophysiology Assistant uses NuPrep first and then the gel.
• “It’s important to have distance between the electrodes so that you don’t create gel
bridges”.
• Neurophysiology Assistant disinfects and puts on ECG (2-system) on the patients,

==PAGE:155==
• Neurophysiology Assistant looks at the patient reference and evaluates while the
patient is relaxing.
• Neurophysiology Assistant reviews EEG while the patient is relaxing and annotates
findings.
• Neurophysiology Assistant also looks at other patient’s data while patient is relaxing.
• Neurophysiology Assistant sometimes does not annotate sinking or deep breaths
which have a visible effect on the EEG - when asked why, they answered, “they look
so much like physiologic artifacts that we are used to so there’s no need to annotate
these. If there’s doubt, the doctor can look at the video”.
• When time is up, Neurophysiology Assistant tells the patient that the examination
is done, and stops the recording - there’s no indication that time is up besides the
timer at the bottom of the screen.
• Neurophysiology Assistant helps the patient taking off the electrodes, ECG, and eye
electrode, and wipe off the majority of the gel.
• Patient states that they nearly fell asleep.
• Neurophysiology Assistant does not annotate if “it looks normal”.
• “In general, it’s better to annotate if in doubt rather than not doing it”.
• “It’s important to respect the time and silence for relaxation as most things happen
when the patient is almost asleep”.

• Patient is asked what they felt during their seizure.
• Patient is asked about their last seizure and if they are taking any medication.
• Patient’s mom is asked whether there is any history with epilepsy in the family.

quency.
• Explains the examination to the patient.
• Neurophysiology Assistant uses their hands to measure the patient’s scalp accord-
ing to the 10-20 system.
• Neurophysiology Assistant has a device connected to the electrodes which gives
a visual overview of the impedance and connection of the electrodes. The device
uses small lights for each electrode which are all switched on - light means no con-
nection/high impedance whereas no light means a good connection/low impedance.
• Neurophysiology Assistant puts on ECG and eye electrode.
• Prepares lamp for photic stimulation, and turns off the lights.
• The light is turned off and the video recording is turned on.
• The patient is asked to close their eyes.
• Recording is started.

A.4
User tests on the BrainCapture application (V1)
A.4.1
User test 14/9
• App UX score (1-5): 4
• User readiness to scan score (1-5): 4.5
Scan 1: 10:11-10:55
• Nr. of errors: 4
• Nr. of questions: 3
• Gel time: 10:13-10:35
• Body language: The user is not “scared” of the equipment but is a little fragile with
the patient.
Notes:
• User wants to start measuring the head for the cap rather than starting the app
• Good patient communication
• Quick to learn by copying the demo
• User forgets to connect the cap and amplifier
• User is a little confused when asked to fill the whole cap (when seeing the corre-
sponding screen) – almost skips the screen
• User finds it difficult to get a feel of how hard they have the press the needle
• User has minor complications with gelling the cap
• User finds that the gel is a good indication of where they are on the cap
• User is good at using the app to check the electrode connection (connection with
cap)
• User strives to get all the electrodes green rather than settling on yellow
• User does not use the NuPrep gel until asked to do so
• User puts ECG stickers on first before connecting the cords thus must remove them
and try again
• User feels that the first eye blink exercise done by the patient was not good enough,
so they restart the exercise to get a better result
• User changes stance when asked
• User starts cleaning while the patient relaxes losing the patient focus and missing
movements
Data-driven optimization of UI & UX
161
==PAGE:169==
• User is unsure about the event icon (the icon is unclear)
• User reads all the text aloud both to themselves and the patient
• User finds the “relax” text confusing and misleading
• User helps the patient clean up
• User remembers to turn everything off and press “Finish”
• Q: How does the calcium in the water affect the cap when being cleaned over time?
Scan 2: 11:05-11:49
• Nr. of errors: 4
• Nr. of questions: 3

it fitting a little tighter

during the scan

Test user 1
Experience as a Nurse: 31 years in intensive care
Number of errors: 6
UI aesthetics score (1-5): 4.5
UX guidance score (1-5): 5
• The user wants to check no in the check boxes on the Patient information screen.
• The user navigates well through the Patient information screen.
• The user puts on the cap right after measuring the patient’s head before it is shown
in the flow.
• The user connects the ECG to the amplifier first before connecting the stickers on
the wire.
• The user puts the ECG on the patient’s wrists before it is shown in the flow.
• When the user sees the “Tap to start” screen, they are confused whether they have
already started the exercise. The user asks for clarification on whether the intended
information text is only for information before the actual exercise starts.
• The user is unsure what the word “annotate” means.
• For the annotation, the user would like to write a comment after clicking the anno-
tation. They explain, ”if I told the patient to keep their eyes open and they for some
reason did not, I would click the eyes open icon and write ”during this session, the
patient started blinking” so that it would be marked in the EEG to get the best result”.
• The user finished the first ”eyes open” part of the eyes exercise and does not notice
that the ”Next” button has changed from its disabled state. Thus, the user does not
click it and is confused.
• The user finishes the ”blink continuously” part of the eyes exercise and then asks the
patient to talk. When asked why they explain, ”the patient was asked to do these
things [eyes open, eyes closed, and blink continuously]... If the three on top are
exercises, then the next three at the bottom are also exercises, is how I understand
it. Also, because in the information text, it says ”the patient has to open, close, and
blink their eyes”, and it says the same in the first three annotations...” They further
explain, ”I remembered from the last test [the user test on the current BrainCapture
application], that we only had to annotate disturbances or artifacts, so that is why I
Data-driven optimization of UI & UX
171
==PAGE:179==
am a little confused... It should be a little more clear that the first three are part of the
exercises while the others are not, because talking could very well be an exercise,

• In regards to editing an annotation, the user states, ”these annotations look like the
exercises, so it is unclear to me where I actually have to edit anything.”
• On the ”Tap for information” screen, the user comments ”compared to the other

focus, so I feel like I have to read everything, so that is nice in this version.”
• Once the eyes exercise is done, the user feels positive when seeing that it has
changed to green in the ”exercise overview” screen.
• The user gets to the ”Tap to start” screen of the hyperventilation exercise, where the
information text is stated. The user notes, ”here, it is a little contradicting as it says

they should always keep their eyes closed. You have to be really sharp in how you

started to later note it down somewhere, so we know exactly how long the seizure

mation that I would ask nearly no matter what I have to do with the patient.”

Test user 16
Experience as a Clinical Nurse Specialist: 5 years at the Respiratory Medical Department
at Hvidovre hospital.
Number of errors: 0
UI aesthetics score (1-5): 5

User readiness to scan score (1-5): 5
• The user navigates easily through the Patient information screen.
• The user navigates easily through the Connect equipment screen.
• The user successfully clicks on the selected cap.
• When the user sees the Tip, the user successfully tells the patient to keep their eyes
closed and open their jaw slightly.
• The user starts the first exercise and sees the exercise information text, and uses it
to introduce the patient to the exercise.
• The user successfully understands the annotation component and annotates when
the patients deviates from the exercises. The user comments, ”it makes very good
sense, also that it counts how many annotations so I have an idea of how much
noise there is during the scan and just to keep track of the progress.”
• The user successfully clicks the ”Try again” button to redo the exercise.
• The user successfully edits an annotation, and notes. The user comments, ”it makes
very good sense with the edit pencil.”
• About the Exercise screen where the first exercise has changed to green after com-
pletion, the user notes ”it very nice that it has a check mark, it is green, and I can
keep going.”
• The user successfully clicks the ”Other” annotation when asked to annotate a cough.
• The user reacts well to the ”Electrode lost connection” alert by saying ”oh there is an
electrode that has lost connection, I will check it.” The user further comments, ”that
made absolute logical sense cause it turns green when the connection is back, so it
is beautiful. It also makes sense in terms of other things we use as nurses for exam-
ple with ECG where it gives a similar warning if the electrode has lost connection,
so it is very familiar for us nurses.”
• The user reacts well to the ”Patient has fallen asleep” alert by waking up the patient.
• The user reacts well to the ”Seizure like behavior has been detected” alert by making
sure the patient is okay and then clicking to annotate it in the app.
